  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer2389137539034828733">من هذا الطفل الذي يناديه الجميع بالشيطان الصغير ويصفونه بقط المزاريب؟ وأي طفل هذا الذي يحمل في قلبه عصفورا يغني؟<br/><br/>"شجرتي شجرة البرتقال الرائعة" للكاتب خوسيه ماورو دي فاسكونسيلوس عمل يدرس في المدارس البرازيلية وينصح الأساتذة في المعاهد الفرنسية طلبتهم بقراءته... إنه عمل مؤثر وإنساني على لسان شاعر طفل لم يتجاوز عمره خمس سنوات... عمل لا يروي حكاية خرافية ولا أحلام الصغار في الب</span>
  <span id="freeText2389137539034828733" style="display:none">من هذا الطفل الذي يناديه الجميع بالشيطان الصغير ويصفونه بقط المزاريب؟ وأي طفل هذا الذي يحمل في قلبه عصفورا يغني؟<br /><br />"شجرتي شجرة البرتقال الرائعة" للكاتب خوسيه ماورو دي فاسكونسيلوس عمل يدرس في المدارس البرازيلية وينصح الأساتذة في المعاهد الفرنسية طلبتهم بقراءته... إنه عمل مؤثر وإنساني على لسان شاعر طفل لم يتجاوز عمره خمس سنوات... عمل لا يروي حكاية خرافية ولا أحلام الصغار في البرازيل فحسب، بل يروي مغامرات الكاتب في طفولته، مغامرات الطفل الذي تعلم القراءة في سن الرابعة دون معلم، الطفل الذي يحمل في قلبه عصفورا وفي رأسه شيطانا يهمس له بأفكار توقعه في المتاعب مع الكبار... هذه رواية عذبة عذوبة نسغ ثمرة برتقال حلوة... رواية إنسانية تصف البراءة التي يمكن لقلب طفل أن يحملها، وتعرفنا إلى روح الشاعر الفطرية... حكاية طفل يحمل دماء سكان البرازيل الأصليين، طفل يسرق كل صباح من حديقة أحد الأثرياء زهرة لأجل معلمته... وهو يتساءل بمنتهى البراءة: ألم يمنح الله الزهور لكل الناس؟".</span>
  <a data-text-id="2389137539034828733" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div id="review_313190873" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/313190873" />
    <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani"><img alt="Ahmad Sharabiani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194930432p2/614778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/313190873?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2012</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer12383731659138939129">O Meu Pe de Laranja Lima = My Sweet Orange Tree (Zeze #1), José Mauro de Vasconcelos<br/><br/>My Sweet Orange Tree, is a novel by José Mauro de Vasconcelos. The book was first published in 1968 and it was used for literature classes for elementary schools in Brazil. Also, it has been translated and published in US and Europe. <br/><br/>The novel is part of a tetralogy written by Vasconcelos and centered on different stages in the life of the protagonist, Zeze, and by extension, Vasconcelos' life as well. The four b</span>
  <span id="freeText12383731659138939129" style="display:none">O Meu Pe de Laranja Lima = My Sweet Orange Tree (Zeze #1), José Mauro de Vasconcelos<br /><br />My Sweet Orange Tree, is a novel by José Mauro de Vasconcelos. The book was first published in 1968 and it was used for literature classes for elementary schools in Brazil. Also, it has been translated and published in US and Europe. <br /><br />The novel is part of a tetralogy written by Vasconcelos and centered on different stages in the life of the protagonist, Zeze, and by extension, Vasconcelos' life as well. The four books were published in a disorganized order, following an aleatory chronology instead of a direct one. The direct continuation of the story, Doidão, was actually published in 1963, five years before My Sweet Orange Tree, and follows the life of Zeze during his adolescence. ...<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: هجدهم دسامبر سال 1988میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: درخت زیبای من؛ اثر: ژوزه مائورو ده واسکونسلوس؛ مترجم: قاسم صنعوی؛ مشخصات نشر تهران، سحر، 1357؛ چاپ دیگر 1367، در 214ص، چاپ پنجم: تهران، راه مانا، 1382؛ در 254ص؛ چاپ هفتم 1387؛ چاپ هشتم 1388؛ چاپ نهم 1389؛ چاپ دوازدهم 1392؛ موضوع داستانهای نویسندگان برزیلی سده 20م<br /><br />عنوان: درخت زیبای من؛ اثر: ژوزه مائورو ده واسکونسلوس؛ مترجم: مهدی شهشهانی؛ مشخصات نشر: تهران، قو، 1383، در 232ص، شابک 9789646412811؛ چاپ دوم 1389؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان برزیلی سده 20م<br /><br />چه نام دشوارخوانی دارد، این نویسنده؛ شاید برای همین باشد که نام ساده تری همچون: «ززه» یا «زی.زی» را برای کودک، برگزیده باشند؛ کتاب، ماجراهای «ژوزه واسکونسلوس»، پسر آقای «پائولو» را روایت می‌کند؛ «زه زه (مخفف ژوزه)» تقریباً پنج ساله‌ است، اما نسبت به سنش پیشرس به شمار می‌آیدد؛ بارزترین وجه شخصیت این کودک، شیطنت‌های باورنکردنی، و توانایی تخیل بی پایان اوست؛ اما به نظر خودش اینها از این ناشی می‌شود که «شیطان توی جلدم رفته‌ است.»؛ فرض خانواده و همسایه‌ ها بر این است، که «زه زه» ذاتاً شرور است، و برای همین است که پسرک مدام کتک می‌خورد؛ رابطه ی «زه زه» با اعضای خانواده «پدر بیکار»، «مادر سرخپوست»، «سه خواهر»، و «یک برادر بزرگتر»، و «یک برادر کوچکتر»؛ بخشی از داستان است؛ «مادر و لالا» کارگری می‌کنند؛ «گلوریا» او را دوست دارد، و «ژاندیرا» او را کتک می‌زند؛ «آنتونیو (توتوکا)» ترسو است، اما گاهی پشتیبان «زه زه»‌ است، و خیلی اوقات پشتش به اوست؛ اما «لوئیس»، «لوئیس» شاه اوست؛ «زه زه» گهگاه واکسی است، و مدتی هم شاگرد فروشنده ی دوره گرد صفحات موسیقی بوده است، «زه زه» در مدرسه، رفتاری دیگرگونه دارد؛ خانم معلم «سیسیلیا پائیم»، که چندان هم زیبا نیست؛ این شاگرد سر به راه، باهوش و ساعی را دوست دارد، و حواسش هست که «زه زه» زنگ‌های تفریح چیزی برای خوردن داشته باشد؛ «زه زه» سینما را هم دوست دارد؛ فیلم‌های وسترن به گسترش دنیای خیال او یاری می‌کند؛ «فرد تامپسون»، «کن مینارد»، و «بیوک جونز» دوستانش هستند، و گاهی به «زه زه»؛ «تفنگ»، «اسب»، و «شلاق» قرض می‌دهند؛ بعدها «زه زه» به فیلم‌های عشقی علاقمند می‌شود، تا ببیند «...؛ دیگران یکدیگر را دوست دارند.»؛ اما سنگ صبور «زه زه»، و گوش شنوای همه ماجراهای او؛ درخت پرتغالش «مینگینهو» است؛ زندگی «زه زه» از زمانی که او با «مانوئل والادارس» آشنا می‌شود، تغییر می‌کند؛ مردی که ماشین قشنگی دارد، و دیگران «پورتوگا (پرتغالی)» صدایش می‌کنند؛ «واسکونسلوس» داستانگوی قهاری ست؛ خیال گسترده و دلانگیزش، ایشان را به سوی نویسندگی راه نمود؛ نخستین رمان «واسکونسلوس»: «موز وحشی در سال 1942میلادی» منتشر شد، اما موفقیت بزرگ ایشان در پهنه ی ادبیات با انتشار: «روزینیا، قایق من»؛ در سال 1962میلادی آشکار شد<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 18/06/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer251584854977961779">This is the first “real” book I remember reading – I also remember crying while I read it. I actually gasped when I came across this title while browsing here on goodreads. Zeze, the five-year-old street wise shoe shiner and his imaginary friend – the orange tree – are as part of me as Harry Potter will one day be part of my children. Zeze though is not fighting with the forces of evil in an imaginary world. His struggles are those of poverty and loneliness, so real to this day yet to children i</span>
  <span id="freeText251584854977961779" style="display:none">This is the first “real” book I remember reading – I also remember crying while I read it. I actually gasped when I came across this title while browsing here on goodreads. Zeze, the five-year-old street wise shoe shiner and his imaginary friend – the orange tree – are as part of me as Harry Potter will one day be part of my children. Zeze though is not fighting with the forces of evil in an imaginary world. His struggles are those of poverty and loneliness, so real to this day yet to children in Brazil and everywhere. Oliver Twist is probably a better comparison than Harry Potter. <br />This book is out of print in English, and it is such a pity, because it is timeless. And because my own children do not read Portuguese. <br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer246834027" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5399194075015226105">The first book (out of two) to EVER make me cry, this one actually made me sob. I can relate to the main character and his little boy's view on the world, his fruitful imagination, and his endless creativity. I believe everyone can see themselves in him, in a way or another. The sad part -no spoiler- is his depression, his hopelessness, his apparently never-ending sadness, and how much tragedies can affect a little child's life when those closest to him are oblivious to what's happening. Teaches</span>
  <span id="freeText5399194075015226105" style="display:none">The first book (out of two) to EVER make me cry, this one actually made me sob. I can relate to the main character and his little boy's view on the world, his fruitful imagination, and his endless creativity. I believe everyone can see themselves in him, in a way or another. The sad part -no spoiler- is his depression, his hopelessness, his apparently never-ending sadness, and how much tragedies can affect a little child's life when those closest to him are oblivious to what's happening. Teaches a great life lesson, a beautiful tale about imaginary friends taken to a whole new level, where a little boy creates his own little world to escape the harsh reality of his real life, and on the way learns the value of true love and friendship in its purest form.</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13198822-settare?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13198822-settare?shelf=latin-america">latin-america</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer423735526" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6047364360351126230">I don't remember much about the details of this book, only that it was a sad, sweet, and deep journey through human emotions. It's a book I think any 12-year-old who can handle it should read. There's a famous word in Portuguese, <i>"Saudade"</i>. This word has been referred to so many times that it's somehow become a part of English, too, or at least I think it's a word whose meaning we should know.<br/>Saudade (n.): <i>Saudade is a deep emotional state of nostalgic or profound melancholic longing for an abse</i></span>
  <span id="freeText6047364360351126230" style="display:none">I don't remember much about the details of this book, only that it was a sad, sweet, and deep journey through human emotions. It's a book I think any 12-year-old who can handle it should read. There's a famous word in Portuguese, <i>"Saudade"</i>. This word has been referred to so many times that it's somehow become a part of English, too, or at least I think it's a word whose meaning we should know.<br />Saudade (n.): <i>Saudade is a deep emotional state of nostalgic or profound melancholic longing for an absent something or someone that one cares for and/or loves. Moreover, it often carries a repressed knowledge that the object of longing might never be had again.</i><br />This book is the embodiment of <i>Saudade</i>.<br /><br /><br />Original review from 2012:<br />نظرم به طور کلی راجع به کتاب: به نظرم ارزش بیش از یک بار خوندن رو حتـما داره.<br />نثر ساده و روان و خیلی خوبی داشت، بعضی جاها توصیف های خیلی قشنگی داشت. نثرش با احساس بود، یعنی می‌تونست به جز وقایع معمولی، احساسات و حالت های شخصیت هاشو به خواننده القا کنه. داستان جذابی هم داشت، یعنی از اون کتابایی که آدم وقتی میگیره دستش نمی‌تونه بذاره زمین. و این که نویسنده خیلی خوب (و نه خیلی مستقیم) مقصودش رو بیان کرده بود. خیلی خوب. دیگه این که پایان غیر قابل پیش‌بینی ای داشت . (و از این خوشم اومد - البته یکم ضد حال هم خوردم) شخصیت اضافه هم توی داستان نداشت . البته به نظرم لالا یه مقدار نقش چغندر رو داشت بین خواهر برادر ها ، ولی کلا شخصیتا به اندازه بودن . واقعیت های اجتماعی رو خیــلی خوب بیان کرده بود ، ( مثلا این که بیایم از دید ِ یه "فقیر" به "فقر" نگاه کنیم ، یا از دید یه بچه‌ای که با خشونت باهاش رفتار میشه به "کودک آزاری" نگاه کنیم ، خیلی فرق داره با دید کلی خودمون از فقر و کودک آزاری و امثال این ها . ) دیگه این که از دوستی ِ راحت ِ یک آدم بزرگ با یک بچه 5 ساله خیلی خوشم اومد . فکر میکنم که این داستانش میتونست توی مکان ها و زمان های دیگه‌ای هم اتفاق بیفته . محدودیت سنی هم نداشت کتابش ؛ برای هرکسی میتونست جذاب باشه .<br />نظرم راجع به شخصیت ها :<br />زه زه ، شخصیت اصلی، خیلی خوب تونسته از زبون خودش، خودش رو برای خواننده توصیف کنه، احساسات و افکارش رو توضیح بده . ذهن خیلی جالبی داشت؛ به چیزایی دقت میکرد که شاید ما وقتی به سنش بودیم کم ترین اهمیت و توجهی هم بهشون نداشتیم، سرگرمی هاش و علایقش، همش، همشون خیلی دوست داشتنی و جالب بودن .<br />خواهر و برادر هاش . لوئیس که واقعا نشانه یک بچه پاک و ساده 2 - 3 ساله بود . گلوریا برخلاف بقیه، میتونست ذهن برادر کوچیکش رو خیلی راحت درک کنه، برای همین هم بود که این قدر بهش کمک میکرد / باهاش مهربون بود به نظرم . توتوکا ، کلا شخصیت مهربون و خوبی داشت فقط اون کتک کاریش با توجه به شخصیتش برام خیلی عجیب بود . لالا که نقش چغندرو ایفا میکرد ؛ ژاندیرا هم زیاد نقش نداشت ولی از همون یه ذره ـش هم خوشم نیومد. (دختره‌ی کودک آزار!)<br />پرتغالی . خیلی کم یابن آدم بزرگ هایی که این قدر قلب مهربانی داشته باشن و به خاطر تنبیه یه بچه پشیمون بشن، و در نهایت وابستگی شدیدی بین آدم بزرگ و بچه هه به وجود بیاد . همین طور آدم بزرگی که بتونه یه بچه 5 ساله رو درک کنه خیـلی کم پیدا میشه . برای همین از شخصیت ِ کم یابش خوشم اومد .<br />یه اشکال هم توی ترجمه کتاب بود ، مثلا مینگینهو باید باشه مینگینیو ! (مثل رونالدینیو ، یکی بگه رونالدینهو مسخرس خب)<br />و از این اسم ها هم تو کتاب زیاد بود.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6047364360351126230" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText9214748104233209509" style="display:none"><br />It is about Zeze a 5-year old kid and his family.<br />Zeze is a devilish kid in everyone’s eyes but in fact he has the purest heart. <br />He tells his orange tree his secrets and adventures and from them you get to know him very well.<br /><br />It was so entertaining to see things from the boy’s perspective and the expressions he used to describe his life were so adorable.<br /><br />I am super glad I picked it yesterday which was one of the most difficult days I have ever. <div id="review_2966377508" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2966377508" />
    <a title="Marie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5157049-marie"><img alt="Marie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588700723p2/5157049.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2966377508?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marie" href="/user/show/5157049-marie">Marie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789500283595" href="/book/show/10200182-mi-planta-de-naranja-lima">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157049-marie?shelf=novel">novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157049-marie?shelf=brazil">brazil</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157049-marie?shelf=realism">realism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2966377508" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9896635033786293388">Read a bunch of reviews here, and you'll get how this is the saddest, most memorable book ever. I mean, it's sad, but I disagree with other people pertaining the value of it. A book can't be rated on its tearjerker-o-metre quality. If that were the case, probably John Green is the greatest author to have walked on Earth. I can't believe this book was candidly offered in schools. <br/><br/>The story follows Zezé, a very poor North Brazilian kid and his family. Having the dynamics of poor people in fiction,</span>
  <span id="freeText9896635033786293388" style="display:none">Read a bunch of reviews here, and you'll get how this is the saddest, most memorable book ever. I mean, it's sad, but I disagree with other people pertaining the value of it. A book can't be rated on its tearjerker-o-metre quality. If that were the case, probably John Green is the greatest author to have walked on Earth. I can't believe this book was candidly offered in schools. <br /><br />The story follows Zezé, a very poor North Brazilian kid and his family. Having the dynamics of poor people in fiction, the story is very reminiscent of Maggie, A Girl of the Streets, except Zezé is 5 years old and unbeliebably "smart", expressive, even if we find later that the narrator survived to adulthood, there are tons of scandalous things on this book that make it more for adults, and less for a school, like the fact that he curses like a sailor, and there are enough allusions to prostitution to rise red flags. A lot of the poverty aspect seems to get included so that we root for Zezé. But am I gonna believe that barely kids do speak about how "Jesus prefers the rich" and "I noticed my teacher was ugly and nobody loved her, so I stole a flower for her"? Hmmm.<br /><br />Honestly, Tom Sawyer is a better choice. Not saying this book doesn't have a few, truly childlike moments, but they are few and far in between.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9896635033786293388" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

        <a title="bookswithgeorgia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="bookswithgeorgia" href="/user/show/112848372-bookswithgeorgia">bookswithgeorgia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781536203288" href="/book/show/38533153-my-sweet-orange-tree">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3452845896" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7696830188870886488">If I had to describe this book in three words: poignant, touching, sobering.<br/><br/>@booksthatgotmeshook bought me this as a surprise because it’s her favourite book ever. Sel... THANK YOU🥺 There’s no way I would have ever reached for this if it weren’t for you! This book was so different from anything I’ve ever read before - it’s such a special one which I will treasure for years to come.<br/><br/>This book is told from the point of view of five year-old Zezé and is SO cleverly written. I literally felt like I l</span>
  <span id="freeText7696830188870886488" style="display:none">If I had to describe this book in three words: poignant, touching, sobering.<br /><br />@booksthatgotmeshook bought me this as a surprise because it’s her favourite book ever. Sel... THANK YOU🥺 There’s no way I would have ever reached for this if it weren’t for you! This book was so different from anything I’ve ever read before - it’s such a special one which I will treasure for years to come.<br /><br />This book is told from the point of view of five year-old Zezé and is SO cleverly written. I literally felt like I lived through every moment and emotion alongside him, and I SO wanted to just reach through the pages and give him a squeeze. Zezé is a beautifully crafted character - he is incredibly intelligent, charismatic and made me smile on a number of occasions with things he came out with, but his circumstances also force him to understand the darkest side of life at a very young age, and he carries the weight of the world on his shoulders which honestly tore me apart.<br /><br />This isn’t a particularly happy read (content warning: suicide, child abuse/beating), but is definitely a thought-provoking one. It made me realise that a lot of subjects that I read about are incredibly trivial, and allowed me to view the world in a way in which I have never had to before. I really think that’s when you know that you’ve read something powerful! I would definitely recommend this book to everybody - the only thing holding me back from giving it 5 stars is that I felt as though as a reader, I had to fill quite a few gaps in in order to be able to understand the story. There were a couple of occasions where I had to pause and consider whether I’d properly understood what I’d just read. I think it’s just a writing style that I’m not really used to, however I think Vasconcelos has done this for a reason, and it’s honestly a very minute ‘criticism’ if you could even call it that! I’m going to leave my review there because I don’t want to give much away - I think it’s important to go into books like these with little prior knowledge!<br /><br />All in all, a beautiful, beautiful book 🍊</span>
  <a data-text-id="7696830188870886488" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4838720622428190618">After finishing a high fantasy book, I wanted to read something light. So, I opted this one...Honestly I didn’t expect much from it, yet I was underwhelmed. I wasn’t attached to the kid nor the plot. I was just reading for the sake of reading, which reminded me about most of the books I read during a school semester. Also, the kid’s maturity of his age bothered me; I have read so many fantasy, hard to believe books, yet this book’s notion of a 5 years old kid to be mature disturbed me.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3333005730" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3333005730" />
    <a title="Dalia Ismail" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15649908-dalia-ismail"><img alt="Dalia Ismail" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356025790p2/15649908.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3333005730?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dalia Ismail" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dalia Ismail" href="/user/show/15649908-dalia-ismail">Dalia Ismail</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789997555625" href="/book/show/46571.My_Sweet_Orange_Tree">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3333005730" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5394855576970949624">A poor family of many kids. An unemployed father. An overworked mother. Debt. Agony. Humility. Shame. Anger. Rage. Sorrow. <br/><br/>This is the setting where Ziza, a small, precocious, malnourished boy of five or six, grows up. He's beaten up and punished for mistakes that no one cares to analyze. He doesn't realize he's a scapegoat, a punching bag for unprocessed emotions and problems he could never have caused. <br/>Yet, despite the injustice casually and unnecessarily inflicted upon him, Ziza is a very emo</span>
  <span id="freeText5394855576970949624" style="display:none">A poor family of many kids. An unemployed father. An overworked mother. Debt. Agony. Humility. Shame. Anger. Rage. Sorrow. <br /><br />This is the setting where Ziza, a small, precocious, malnourished boy of five or six, grows up. He's beaten up and punished for mistakes that no one cares to analyze. He doesn't realize he's a scapegoat, a punching bag for unprocessed emotions and problems he could never have caused. <br />Yet, despite the injustice casually and unnecessarily inflicted upon him, Ziza is a very emotionally intelligent boy for his age. The Christmas incident is a fair demonstration, but he shows emotional maturity in many other instances as well. Yes, he's just a kid, but poverty taught him a lot about the adult world already. <br /><br />I don't think I enjoyed reading the Arabic translation a lot or the general storyline, but the story nonetheless made me reflect on the millions of children who grow up in similar or far worse conditions all over the world. Their private domestic lives, their imagination and aspirations and emotions. They're only given a voice in works of art. It's a fact that we adults just live with. <br /><br />I wish more of us are like the characters who were empathetic to Ziza. I wish we are more human.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5394855576970949624" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rww/8Yvk7mhCkHNYmVPhsYxlHfz/zskRoammMeMvCPGVKlYjMLonAOW7xzluputuWjr6NDFDR3b61+CALmz6aw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+9pWWQs7YNaupsLnwcVxAx607OKV30dTcxGFdmo/hIXB/D+LsGWpvgmNdoY2MHvcyOsLKltSyTQob8PHp3x2Hw==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/30091.Jos_Mauro_de_Vasconcelos">About José Mauro de Vasconcelos</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/30091.Jos_Mauro_de_Vasconcelos"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1421613463p3/30091.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/30091.Jos_Mauro_de_Vasconcelos">José Mauro de Vasconcelos

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer621987344057773552">José Mauro was born in Rio de Janeiro on February 26 of 1920. His family was very poor, and when he was still very young, he migrated to Natal where relatives took care of him. Entering the Medical Faculty, José abandoned the course of studies in his second year and returned to Rio de Janeiro.[citation needed] There he worked as a boxing instructor and even as a painter's model.<br/><br/>José iniciated his </span>
  <span id="freeText621987344057773552" style="display:none">José Mauro was born in Rio de Janeiro on February 26 of 1920. His family was very poor, and when he was still very young, he migrated to Natal where relatives took care of him. Entering the Medical Faculty, José abandoned the course of studies in his second year and returned to Rio de Janeiro.[citation needed] There he worked as a boxing instructor and even as a painter's model.<br /><br />José iniciated his literature with the novel Banana Brava. His greatest success was his novel Meu Pé de Laranja Lima, that tells about his own personal experiences and the shocks he suffered in his childhood with the abrupt changes of life.<br /><br />José was part Indian and part Portuguese. He passed his childhood in Natal. When he was 9 years old, he learned to swim, and with pleasure he still remembers the days when he threw himself to the waters of the Potengi River to train for swimming competitions. José frequently went to the sea. He won many swimming competitions and, like every boy, liked to play soccer and to climb on trees. José's first job, from 16 yars old to 17 years old, was a sparring partner of featherweight boxers. Next, he worked in a farm in Mazomba, his job was to carry bananas. After that, he became a fisherman and lived on the coastline at Rio de Janeiro. Later he moved to Recife, where he became an elementary teacher and teacher at a fishermen's center.<br /><br />Because of his prodigious capacity of telling stories, possessing a fabulous memory, brilliant imagination, and a large human experience, José felt he was obligated to become an author, and started to write novels when he was 22 years old.<br /><br />The author had his original methods of writing. In the beginning, he would choose the scenarios where the characters would move. Then he would transfer to this place and do rigorous studies there. To write the novel Arara Vermelha, José traveled 450 leagues in the brute wilderness. Next, he builds all the novel, determining even the sentences of the dialogues. He had a memory that, for a long time, allowed him to remember every little detail of his studied scenario. "When the story is entirely made in imagination", reveals the author, "is when I begin to write. I only work I have the impression that the novel is exiting from all the pores of the body."<br /><br />José relates that after finishing writing the first chapter, he passes to the conclusion of the novel, without even elaborating the plot. "That, he explains "because all the chapters are already produced mentally. It is not really important writing a sequence, like alterating the order. In the end everything goes well". José was a cinemactor and worked in films such as Carteira Modelo 19, Fronteiras do Inferno, Floradas na Serra, Canto do Mar (of which he wrote the screenplay), Na Garganta do Diabo, and A Ilha. He won many prizes, such as the Saci prize to best supporting actor, the Saci prize to the best actor of the year, and the Governo do Estado prize to best actor of the year. His novels Arara Vermelha and Vazante were filmed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="621987344057773552" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;دیگر به راستی می دانستم درد یعنی چه. درد به معنای کتک خوردن تا حد بیهوشی نبود. بریدن پا بر اثر یک تکه شیشه و بخیه زدن در داروخانه نبود. درد یعنی چیزی که دل آدم را در هم می شکند و انسان ناگزیر است با آن بمیرد بدون آنکه بتواند رازش را برای کسی تعریف کند.، دردی که انسان را بدون قدرت دست و سر باقی می گذارد و انسان حتی یارای آن را ندارد که سرش را روی بالشت حرکت دهد. &rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/214585">94 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;در خانه ما فقر به اندازه ای بود که آدم خیلی زود یاد می گرفت چیزی را تلف نکند، هرچیزی پول می برد، گران بود.&rdquo;</span>
